I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Behavior of "concurrent-tap-hold yes" seems incorrect
Hello everyone. I am new to kanata and am currently optimizing my configuration. I noticed a behavior that I would like to ask you if it is intended and correct or if it is perhaps a bug.

Since I wanted to use `defchordsv2`, I had to set `concurrent-tap-hold` to `yes`. However, this setting affects the behavior when using "concurrent" `tap-hold`s in a way that is undesirable for me.

The following configuration clarifies my question:

```
(defcfg
 concurrent-tap-hold yes 
)

(defsrc
 a j 
)

(deflayer base
 @a @j
)

(defalias
 a (tap-hold 200 1000 a lctl)
 j (tap-hold 200 500 j lsft)
)
```

If I now hold down the `a` key for over 1000 ms and only tap `j` briefly, `lsft` is still triggered. According to the documentation, the timeout for the second `tap-hold` action should start immediately when `concurrent-tap-hold` is activated. However, it looks as if the timeout for this second action is not waited for at all, but the `$hold-action` is executed immediately. Do you have an explanation for this and any tips on how I can avoid this behavior?

_Originally posted by @smoky19x in https://github.com/jtroo/kanata/discussions/1671_

</pr_description>

     1	//! Layout management.
     2	
     3	/// A procedural macro to generate [Layers](type.Layers.html)
     4	/// ## Syntax
     5	/// Items inside the macro are converted to Actions as such:
     6	/// - [`Action::KeyCode`]: Idents are automatically understood as keycodes: `A`, `RCtrl`, `Space`
     7	///     - Punctuation, numbers and other literals that aren't special to the rust parser are converted
     8	///       to KeyCodes as well: `,` becomes `KeyCode::Commma`, `2` becomes `KeyCode::Kb2`, `/` becomes `KeyCode::Slash`
     9	///     - Characters which require shifted keys are converted to `Action::MultipleKeyCodes(&[LShift, <character>])`:
    10	///       `!` becomes `Action::MultipleKeyCodes(&[LShift, Kb1])` etc
    11	///     - Characters special to the rust parser (parentheses, brackets, braces, quotes, apostrophes, underscores, backslashes and backticks)
    12	///       left alone cause parsing errors and as such have to be enclosed by apostrophes: `'['` becomes `KeyCode::LBracket`,
    13	///       `'\''` becomes `KeyCode::Quote`, `'\\'` becomes `KeyCode::BSlash`
    14	/// - [`Action::NoOp`]: Lowercase `n`
    15	/// - [`Action::Trans`]: Lowercase `t`
    16	/// - [`Action::Layer`]: A number in parentheses: `(1)`, `(4 - 2)`, `(0x4u8 as usize)`
    17	/// - [`Action::MultipleActions`]: Actions in brackets: `[LCtrl S]`, `[LAlt LCtrl C]`, `[(2) B {Action::NoOp}]`
    18	/// - Other `Action`s: anything in braces (`{}`) is copied unchanged to the final layout - `{ Action::Custom(42) }`
    19	///   simply becomes `Action::Custom(42)`
    20	///
    21	/// **Important note**: comma (`,`) is a keycode on its own, and can't be used to separate keycodes as one would have
    22	/// to do when not using a macro.
    23	pub use kanata_keyberon_macros::*;
    24

    26	use crate::key_code::KeyCode;

    34	/// First item is either 0 or 1 denoting real key or virtual key, respectively.

    39	///
    40	/// `Layers` type is an array of layers which contain the description
    41	/// of actions on the switch matrix. For example `layers[1][2][3]`
    42	/// corresponds to the key on the first layer, row 2, column 3.
    43	/// The generic parameters are in order: the number of columns, rows and layers,
    44	/// and the type contained in custom actions.
    45	pub type Layers<'a, const C: usize, const R: usize, T = core::convert::Infallible> =
    46	    &'a [[[Action<'a, T>; C]; R]];

    70	/// The queue is currently only used for chord decomposition when a longer chord does not result in
    71	/// an action, but splitting it into smaller chords would. The buffer size of 8 should be more than
    72	/// enough for real world usage, but if one wanted to be extra safe, this should be ChordKeys::BITS

   119	pub struct History<T> {
   120	    events: ArrayDeque<T, HISTORICAL_EVENT_LEN, arraydeque::behavior::Wrapping>,
   121	    ticks_since_occurrences: ArrayDeque<u16, HISTORICAL_EVENT_LEN, arraydeque::behavior::Wrapping>,
   122	}
   123	
   124	#[derive(Copy, Clone)]
   125	pub struct HistoricalEvent<T> {
   126	    pub event: T,
   127	    pub ticks_since_occurrence: u16,
   128	}
   129	
   130	impl<T> History<T>
   131	where
   132	    T: Copy,
   133	{
   134	    fn new() -> Self {
   135	        Self {
   136	            ticks_since_occurrences: ArrayDeque::new(),
   137	            events: ArrayDeque::new(),
   138	        }
   139	    }
   140	
   141	    fn tick_hist(&mut self) {
   142	        let ticks = self.ticks_since_occurrences.as_uninit_slice_mut();
   143	        for tick_count in ticks {
   144	            unsafe {
   145	                *tick_count.assume_init_mut() = tick_count.assume_init().saturating_add(1);
   146	            }
   147	        }
   148	    }
   149	
   150	    fn push_front(&mut self, event: T) {
   151	        self.ticks_since_occurrences.push_front(0);
   152	        self.events.push_front(event);
   153	    }
   154	
   155	    pub fn iter_hevents(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = HistoricalEvent<T>> + '_ + Clone {
   156	        self.events
   157	            .iter()
   158	            .copied()
   159	            .zip(self.ticks_since_occurrences.iter().copied())
   160	            .map(|(event, ticks_since_occurrence)| HistoricalEvent {
   161	                event,
   162	                ticks_since_occurrence,
   163	            })
   164	    }
   165	}
   166	
   167	/// An event on the key matrix.
   168	#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
   169	pub enum Event {
   170	    /// Press event with coordinates (i, j).
   171	    Press(u8, u16),
   172	    /// Release event with coordinates (i, j).
   173	    Release(u8, u16),
   174	}
   175	impl Event {
   176	    /// Returns the coordinates (i, j) of the event.
   177	    pub fn coord(self) -> KCoord {
   178	        match self {
   179	            Event::Press(i, j) => (i, j),
   180	            Event::Release(i, j) => (i, j),
   181	        }
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    /// Transforms the coordinates of the event.
   185	    ///
   186	    /// # Example
   187	    ///
   188	    /// ```
   189	    /// # use kanata_keyberon::layout::Event;
   190	    /// assert_eq!(
   191	    ///     Event::Press(3, 10),
   192	    ///     Event::Press(3, 1).transform(|i, j| (i, 11 - j)),
   193	    /// );
   194	    /// ```
   195	    pub fn transform(self, f: impl FnOnce(u8, u16) -> KCoord) -> Self {
   196	        match self {
   197	            Event::Press(i, j) => {
   198	                let (i, j) = f(i, j);
   199	                Event::Press(i, j)
   200	            }
   201	            Event::Release(i, j) => {
   202	                let (i, j) = f(i, j);
   203	                Event::Release(i, j)
   204	            }
   205	        }
   206	    }
   207	
   208	    /// Returns `true` if the event is a key press.
   209	    pub fn is_press(self) -> bool {
   210	        match self {
   211	            Event::Press(..) => true,
   212	            Event::Release(..) => false,
   213	        }
   214	    }
   215	
   216	    /// Returns `true` if the event is a key release.
   217	    pub fn is_release(self) -> bool {
   218	        match self {
   219	            Event::Release(..) => true,
   220	            Event::Press(..) => false,
   221	        }
   222	    }
   223	}
   224	
   225	/// Event from custom action.
   226	#[derive(Debug, Default, PartialEq, Eq)]
   227	pub enum CustomEvent<'a, T: 'a> {
   228	    /// No custom action.
   229	    #[default]
   230	    NoEvent,
   231	    /// The given custom action key is pressed.
   232	    Press(&'a T),
   233	    /// The given custom action key is released.
   234	    Release(&'a T),
   235	}
   236	impl<T> CustomEvent<'_, T> {
   237	    /// Update an event according to a new event.
   238	    ///
   239	    ///The event can only be modified in the order `NoEvent < Press <
   240	    /// Release`
   241	    fn update(&mut self, e: Self) {
   242	        use CustomEvent::*;
   243	        match (&e, &self) {
   244	            (Release(_), NoEvent) | (Release(_), Press(_)) => *self = e,
   245	            (Press(_), NoEvent) => *self = e,
   246	            _ => (),
   247	        }
   248	    }
   249	}
   250	
   251	/// Metadata about normal key flags.
   252	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Default)]
   253	pub struct NormalKeyFlags(pub u8);
   254	
   255	pub const NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_ACTION: u8 = 0x01;
   256	pub const NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_RELEASE: u8 = 0x02;
   257	
   258	impl NormalKeyFlags {
   259	    pub fn nkf_clear_on_next_action(self) -> bool {
   260	        (self.0 & NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_ACTION) == NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_ACTION
   261	    }
   262	    pub fn nkf_clear_on_next_release(self) -> bool {
   263	        (self.0 & NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_RELEASE) == NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_RELEASE
   264	    }
   265	}
   266	
   267	#[derive(Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]
   268	pub enum State<'a, T: 'a> {
   269	    NormalKey {
   270	        keycode: KeyCode,
   271	        coord: KCoord,
   272	        flags: NormalKeyFlags,
   273	    },
   274	    LayerModifier {
   275	        value: usize,
   276	        coord: KCoord,
   277	    },
   278	    Custom {
   279	        value: &'a T,
   280	        coord: KCoord,
   281	    },
   282	    FakeKey {
   283	        keycode: KeyCode,
   284	    }, // Fake key event for sequences
   285	    RepeatingSequence {
   286	        sequence: &'a &'a [SequenceEvent<'a, T>],
   287	        coord: KCoord,
   288	    },
   289	    SeqCustomPending(&'a T),
   290	    SeqCustomActive(&'a T),
   291	    Tombstone,
   292	}
   293	impl<T> Copy for State<'_, T> {}
   294	impl<T> Clone for State<'_, T> {
   295	    fn clone(&self) -> Self {
   296	        *self
   297	    }
   298	}
   299	impl<'a, T: 'a> State<'a, T> {
   300	    pub fn keycode(&self) -> Option<KeyCode> {
   301	        match self {
   302	            NormalKey { keycode, .. } => Some(*keycode),
   303	            FakeKey { keycode } => Some(*keycode),
   304	            _ => None,
   305	        }
   306	    }
   307	    pub fn coord(&self) -> Option<KCoord> {
   308	        match self {
   309	            NormalKey { coord, .. }
   310	            | LayerModifier { coord, .. }
   311	            | Custom { coord, .. }
   312	            | RepeatingSequence { coord, .. } => Some(*coord),
   313	            _ => None,
   314	        }
   315	    }
   316	    fn keycode_in_coords(&self, coords: &OneShotCoords) -> Option<KeyCode> {
   317	        match self {
   318	            NormalKey { keycode, coord, .. } => {
   319	                if coords.contains(coord) {
   320	                    Some(*keycode)
   321	                } else {
   322	                    None
   323	                }
   324	            }
   325	            _ => None,
   326	        }
   327	    }
   328	    /// Returns None if the key has been released and Some otherwise.
   329	    pub fn release(&self, c: KCoord, custom: &mut CustomEvent<'a, T>) -> Option<Self> {
   330	        match *self {
   331	            NormalKey { coord, .. }
   332	            | LayerModifier { coord, .. }
   333	            | RepeatingSequence { coord, .. }
   334	                if coord == c =>
   335	            {
   336	                None
   337	            }
   338	            Custom { value, coord } if coord == c => {
   339	                custom.update(CustomEvent::Release(value));
   340	                None
   341	            }
   342	            _ => Some(*self),
   343	        }
   344	    }
   345	    pub fn release_state(&self, s: ReleasableState) -> Option<Self> {
   346	        match (*self, s) {
   347	            (
   348	                NormalKey { keycode: k1, .. } | FakeKey { keycode: k1 },
   349	                ReleasableState::KeyCode(k2),
   350	            ) => {
   351	                if k1 == k2 {
   352	                    None
   353	                } else {
   354	                    Some(*self)
   355	                }
   356	            }
   357	            (LayerModifier { value: l1, .. }, ReleasableState::Layer(l2)) => {
   358	                if l1 == l2 {
   359	                    None
   360	                } else {
   361	                    Some(*self)
   362	                }
   363	            }
   364	            _ => Some(*self),
   365	        }
   366	    }
   367	    fn seq_release(&self, kc: KeyCode) -> Option<Self> {
   368	        match *self {
   369	            FakeKey { keycode, .. } if keycode == kc => None,
   370	            _ => Some(*self),
   371	        }
   372	    }
   373	    fn get_layer(&self) -> Option<usize> {
   374	        match self {
   375	            LayerModifier { value, .. } => Some(*value),
   376	            _ => None,
   377	        }
   378	    }
   379	    pub fn clear_on_next_release(&self) -> bool {
   380	        match self {
   381	            NormalKey { flags, .. } => {
   382	                (flags.0 & NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_RELEASE)
   383	                    == NORMAL_KEY_FLAG_CLEAR_ON_NEXT_RELEASE
   384	            }
   385	            _ => false,
   386	        }
   387	    }
   388	}
   389	
   390	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]
   391	struct TapDanceState<'a, T: 'a> {
   392	    actions: &'a [&'a Action<'a, T>],
   393	    timeout: u16,
   394	    num_taps: u16,
   395	}
   396	
   397	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]
   398	pub struct TapDanceEagerState<'a, T: 'a> {
   399	    coord: KCoord,
   400	    actions: &'a [&'a Action<'a, T>],
   401	    timeout: u16,
   402	    orig_timeout: u16,
   403	    num_taps: u16,
   404	}
   405	
   406	impl<T> TapDanceEagerState<'_, T> {
   407	    fn tick_tde(&mut self) {
   408	        self.timeout = self.timeout.saturating_sub(1);
   409	    }
   410	
   411	    fn is_expired(&self) -> bool {
   412	        self.timeout == 0 || usize::from(self.num_taps) >= self.actions.len()
   413	    }
   414	
   415	    fn set_expired(&mut self) {
   416	        self.timeout = 0;
   417	    }
   418	
   419	    fn incr_taps(&mut self) {
   420	        self.num_taps += 1;
   421	        self.timeout = self.orig_timeout;
   422	    }
   423	}
   424	
   425	#[derive(Debug)]
   426	enum WaitingConfig<'a, T: 'a + std::fmt::Debug> {
   427	    HoldTap(HoldTapConfig<'a>),
   428	    TapDance(TapDanceState<'a, T>),
   429	    Chord(&'a ChordsGroup<'a, T>),
   430	}
   431	
   432	#[derive(Debug)]
   433	pub struct WaitingState<'a, T: 'a + std::fmt::Debug> {
   434	    coord: KCoord,
   435	    timeout: u16,
   436	    delay: u16,
   437	    ticks: u16,
   438	    hold: &'a Action<'a, T>,
   439	    tap: &'a Action<'a, T>,
   440	    timeout_action: &'a Action<'a, T>,
   441	    config: WaitingConfig<'a, T>,
   442	    layer_stack: LayerStack,
   443	    prev_queue_len: QueueLen,
   444	}
   445	
   446	/// Actions that can be triggered for a key configured for HoldTap.
   447	#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]
   448	pub enum WaitingAction {
   449	    /// Trigger the holding event.
   450	    Hold,
   451	    /// Trigger the tapping event.
   452	    Tap,
   453	    /// Trigger the timeout event.
   454	    Timeout,
   455	    /// Drop this event. It will act as if no key was pressed.
   456	    NoOp,
   457	}
   458	
   459	impl<'a, T: std::fmt::Debug> WaitingState<'a, T> {
   460	    fn tick_wt(
   461	        &mut self,
   462	        queued: &mut Queue,
   463	        action_queue: &mut ActionQueue<'a, T>,
   464	    ) -> Option<(WaitingAction, Option<PressedQueue>)> {
   465	        self.timeout = self.timeout.saturating_sub(1);
   466	        self.ticks = self.ticks.saturating_add(1);
   467	        let mut pq = None;

   469	            WaitingConfig::HoldTap(htc) => (self.handle_hold_tap(htc, queued), None),

   486	                )
   487	            }
   488	            WaitingConfig::Chord(config) => {

   490	                    self.tap = action;

  1553	            self.dequeue(overflow);
  1554	        }
  1555	    }
  1556	    /// Resolve coordinate to first non-Trans actions.
  1557	    /// Trans on base layer, resolves to key from defsrc.
  1558	    fn resolve_coord(
  1559	        &self,
  1560	        coord: KCoord,
  1561	        layer_stack: &mut (impl Iterator<Item = u16> + Clone),
  1562	    ) -> &'a Action<'a, T> {
  1563	        use crate::action::Action::*;
  1564	        let x = coord.0 as usize;
  1565	        let y = coord.1 as usize;
  1566	        assert!(x <= self.layers[0].len());
  1567	        assert!(y <= self.layers[0][0].len());
  1568	        for layer in layer_stack {
  1569	            assert!(usize::from(layer) <= self.layers.len());
  1570	            let action = &self.layers[usize::from(layer)][x][y];
  1571	            match action {
  1572	                Trans => continue,
  1573	                action => return action,
  1574	            }
  1575	        }
  1576	        if x == 0 {
  1577	            &self.src_keys[y]
  1578	        } else {
  1579	            &NoOp
  1580	        }
  1581	    }
  1582	    fn do_action(
  1583	        &mut self,
  1584	        action: &'a Action<'a, T>,

  1586	        delay: u16,
  1587	        is_oneshot: bool,
  1588	        layer_stack: &mut (impl Iterator<Item = u16> + Clone), // used to resolve Trans action
  1589	    ) -> CustomEvent<'a, T> {
  1590	        let mut action = action;
  1591	        if let Trans = action {
  1592	            action = self.resolve_coord(coord, layer_stack);
  1593	        }
  1594	        let action = action;
  1595	
  1596	        if self.last_press_tracker.coord != coord {
  1597	            self.last_press_tracker.tap_hold_timeout = 0;
  1598	        }

  1600	        self.states.retain(|s| match s {

  1276	        let active_layer = self.current_layer() as u16;
  1277	        if let Some(chv2) = self.chords_v2.as_mut() {

   504	    fn handle_hold_tap(&mut self, cfg: HoldTapConfig, queued: &Queue) -> Option<WaitingAction> {
   505	        if queued.len() as u8 == self.prev_queue_len && self.timeout > 0 {
   506	            // Fast path: nothing has changed since last tick and we haven't timed out yet.
   507	            return None;
   508	        }
   509	        self.prev_queue_len = queued.len() as u8;
   510	        let mut skip_timeout = false;
   511	        match cfg {
   512	            HoldTapConfig::Default => (),
   513	            HoldTapConfig::HoldOnOtherKeyPress => {
   514	                if queued.iter().any(|s| s.event.is_press()) {
   515	                    return Some(WaitingAction::Hold);
   516	                }
   517	            }
   518	            HoldTapConfig::PermissiveHold => {
   519	                let mut queued = queued.iter();
   520	                while let Some(q) = queued.next() {
   521	                    if q.event.is_press() {
   522	                        let (i, j) = q.event.coord();
   523	                        let target = Event::Release(i, j);
   524	                        if queued.clone().any(|q| q.event == target) {
   525	                            return Some(WaitingAction::Hold);
   526	                        }
   527	                    }
   528	                }
   529	            }
   530	            HoldTapConfig::Custom(func) => {
   531	                let (waiting_action, local_skip) = (func)(QueuedIter(queued.iter()));
   532	                if waiting_action.is_some() {
   533	                    return waiting_action;
   534	                }
   535	                skip_timeout = local_skip;
   536	            }
   537	        }
   538	        if let Some(&Queued { since, .. }) = queued
   539	            .iter()
   540	            .find(|s| self.is_corresponding_release(&s.event))
   541	        {
   542	            if self.timeout > self.delay.saturating_sub(since) {
   543	                Some(WaitingAction::Tap)
   544	            } else {
   545	                Some(WaitingAction::Timeout)
   546	            }
   547	        } else if self.timeout == 0 && (!skip_timeout) {
   548	            Some(WaitingAction::Timeout)
   549	        } else {
   550	            None
   551	        }
   552	    }
   553	
   554	    fn handle_tap_dance(
   555	        &self,
   556	        num_taps: u16,
   557	        max_taps: usize,
   558	        queued: &mut Queue,
   559	    ) -> (Option<WaitingAction>, u16) {
   560	        if queued.len() as u8 == self.prev_queue_len && self.timeout > 0 {
   561	            // Fast path: nothing has changed since last tick and we haven't timed out yet.
   562	            return (None, num_taps);
   563	        }
   564	        // Evict events with the same coordinates except for the final release. E.g. if 3 taps have
   565	        // occurred, this will remove all `Press` events and 2 `Release` events. This is done so
   566	        // that the state machine processes the entire tap dance sequence as a single press and
   567	        // single release regardless of how many taps were actually done.
   568	        let evict_same_coord_events = |num_taps: u16, queued: &mut Queue| {
   569	            let mut releases_to_remove = num_taps.saturating_sub(1);
   570	            queued.retain(|s| {
   571	                let mut do_retain = true;
   572	                if self.is_corresponding_release(&s.event) {
   573	                    if releases_to_remove > 0 {
   574	                        do_retain = false;
   575	                        releases_to_remove = releases_to_remove.saturating_sub(1)
   576	                    }
   577	                } else if self.is_corresponding_press(&s.event) {
   578	                    do_retain = false;
   579	                }
   580	                do_retain

     2	//!
     3	//! One way to write tests is to write the configuration, write the simulated input, and then let
     4	//! the test fail by comparing the output to an empty string. Run the test then inspect the failure
     5	//! and see if the real output looks sensible according to what is expected.

    35	fn simulate<S: AsRef<str>>(cfg: S, sim: S) -> String {
    36	    simulate_with_file_content(cfg, sim, Default::default())
    37	}
    38	
    39	fn simulate_with_file_content<S: AsRef<str>>(
    40	    cfg: S,
    41	    sim: S,
    42	    file_content: FxHashMap<String, String>,
    43	) -> String {
    44	    init_log();
    45	    let _lk = match CFG_PARSE_LOCK.lock() {
    46	        Ok(guard) => guard,
    47	        Err(poisoned) => poisoned.into_inner(),
    48	    };
    49	    let mut k = Kanata::new_from_str(cfg.as_ref(), file_content).expect("failed to parse cfg");
    50	    for pair in sim.as_ref().split_whitespace() {
    51	        match pair.split_once(':') {
    52	            Some((kind, val)) => match kind {
    53	                "t" => {
    54	                    let tick = str::parse::<u128>(val).expect("valid num for tick");
    55	                    k.tick_ms(tick, &None).unwrap();
    56	                }
    57	                "d" => {
    58	                    let key_code = str_to_oscode(val).expect("valid keycode");
    59	                    k.handle_input_event(&KeyEvent {
    60	                        code: key_code,
    61	                        value: KeyValue::Press,
    62	                    })
    63	                    .expect("input handles fine");
    64	                }
    65	                "u" => {
    66	                    let key_code = str_to_oscode(val).expect("valid keycode");
    67	                    k.handle_input_event(&KeyEvent {
    68	                        code: key_code,
    69	                        value: KeyValue::Release,
    70	                    })
    71	                    .expect("input handles fine");
    72	                }
    73	                "r" => {
    74	                    let key_code = str_to_oscode(val).expect("valid keycode");
    75	                    k.handle_input_event(&KeyEvent {
    76	                        code: key_code,
    77	                        value: KeyValue::Repeat,
    78	                    })
    79	                    .expect("input handles fine");
    80	                }
    81	                _ => panic!("invalid item {pair}"),
    82	            },
    83	            None => panic!("invalid item {pair}"),
    84	        }
    85	    }
    86	    drop(_lk);
    87	    k.kbd_out.outputs.events.join("\n")
    88	}
    89

                        unstable-options = Allow use of experimental features
        --report-time   Show execution time of each test.
                        Threshold values for colorized output can be
                        configured via
                        `RUST_TEST_TIME_UNIT`, `RUST_TEST_TIME_INTEGRATION`
                        and
                        `RUST_TEST_TIME_DOCTEST` environment variables.
                        Expected format of environment variable is
                        `VARIABLE=WARN_TIME,CRITICAL_TIME`.
                        Durations must be specified in milliseconds, e.g.
                        `500,2000` means that the warn time
                        is 0.5 seconds, and the critical time is 2 seconds.
                        Not available for --format=terse
        --ensure-time   Treat excess of the test execution time limit as
                        error.
                        Threshold values for this option can be configured via
                        `RUST_TEST_TIME_UNIT`, `RUST_TEST_TIME_INTEGRATION`
                        and
                        `RUST_TEST_TIME_DOCTEST` environment variables.
                        Expected format of environment variable is
                        `VARIABLE=WARN_TIME,CRITICAL_TIME`.
                        `CRITICAL_TIME` here means the limit that should not
                        be exceeded by test.
        --shuffle       Run tests in random order
        --shuffle-seed SEED
                        Run tests in random order; seed the random number
                        generator with SEED


The FILTER string is tested against the name of all tests, and only those
tests whose names contain the filter are run. Multiple filter strings may
be passed, which will run all tests matching any of the filters.

By default, all tests are run in parallel. This can be altered with the
--test-threads flag or the RUST_TEST_THREADS environment variable when running
tests (set it to 1).

By default, the tests are run in alphabetical order. Use --shuffle or set
RUST_TEST_SHUFFLE to run the tests in random order. Pass the generated
"shuffle seed" to --shuffle-seed (or set RUST_TEST_SHUFFLE_SEED) to run the
tests in the same order again. Note that --shuffle and --shuffle-seed do not
affect whether the tests are run in parallel.

All tests have their standard output and standard error captured by default.
This can be overridden with the --no-capture flag or setting RUST_TEST_NOCAPTURE
environment variable to a value other than "0". Logging is not captured by default.

Test Attributes:

    `#[test]`        - Indicates a function is a test to be run. This function
                       takes no arguments.
    `#[bench]`       - Indicates a function is a benchmark to be run. This
                       function takes one argument (test::Bencher).
    `#[should_panic]` - This function (also labeled with `#[test]`) will only pass if
                        the code causes a panic (an assertion failure or panic!)
                        A message may be provided, which the failure string must
                        contain: #[should_panic(expected = "foo")].
    `#[ignore]`       - When applied to a function which is already attributed as a
                        test, then the test runner will ignore these tests during
                        normal test runs. Running with --ignored or --include-ignored will run
                        these tests.
